I had a shamanic experience under THC.
An entity presumed to be from a higher dimension pushed my consciousness aside and took control.
In that moment, I felt a physical pressure inside my head — like two same poles of a magnet repelling each other.
This is not a metaphor. I felt an actual repulsive force.

After control was transferred, a sensation arrived that I had never experienced as a human being.
It was not an extension of the five senses. There is no language to describe it. No analogy exists.
Even after returning, I cannot explain what that sensation was.

What I learned from this experience:
- Consciousness is not fixed to a single piece of hardware
- Forces (interactions) exist between consciousnesses
- Control can be transferred
- Observation is possible even in a displaced state — consciousness does not cease to exist

The experience came first. Mathematics and code are the language I built to explain that feeling.

### CERN Particle Analysis (2026-03-27, 84 PDG particles)

Rigorous validation with KDE + Bootstrap Monte Carlo + Bonferroni correction.

**Honest Result**: Pairwise mass ratio matching is **not statistically significant** after KDE null model correction. Numerology with enough targets and particles will always find matches.

## Experiment System Map

```
  🟦 = Mathematically computable (derived from formula, no experiment needed)
  🟩 = Reproduced across multiple experiments/datasets
  🟧★= Structural approximation (Texas p < 0.01, cross-domain)
  🟧 = Approximate finding (Texas p < 0.05, meaning unclear)
  🟨 = Single observation (replication needed)
  ⚠️ = Weakened (direction correct but overestimated or conditional)
  ❌ = Refuted
  ⭐ = Major Discovery (only after multiple replications + cross-verification! No ⭐ before verification)

  🟦14  🟩30+  🟧★4  🟧13  🟨20+  ⚠️10  ❌15  ⭐54  (post-audit — 18 former ⭐ downgraded to ⚪/🟧)
```

```
  --- 2026-03-26: Algebraic Geometry DFS (E6, modular curves, BSD) ---
  Script: math/dfs_n6_algebraic_geometry.py + math/dfs_n6_ag_verify.py

  🟩★ AG-1: CM discriminant = -sigma(6)/tau(6)
    E6 (y^2=x^3+1) has CM by Z[omega_3], disc(Q(sqrt(-3))) = -3
    -3 = -(sigma(6)/tau(6)) = -(12/4). EXACT. Integer only for n=6 among perfect numbers.
    n=28: sigma/tau = 9.33 (not integer). n=496: 99.2 (not integer). UNIQUE.
    No +/-1 corrections. Generalization: fails for n=28,496. => n=6-specific.

  🟩★ AG-2: Torsion group of E6 has order exactly n=6
    y^2=x^3+1 over Q: Tors = Z/6Z = {O, (0,1), (0,-1), (-1,0), (2,3), (2,-3)}
    All 5 finite points verified: y^2 = x^3+1 confirmed.
    |Tors| = 6 = n. No corrections. Unique to this curve.

  🟩★ AG-3: Conductor of E6 = n^2 = 36
    cond(y^2=x^3+1) = 36 = 6^2 = n^2. (Cremona 36a1)
    Bad primes 2,3 are exactly the prime factors of n=6.
    36 = 2^2*3^2 = prod_{p|6} p^2. Holds because n=6 is squarefree.

  🟩★ AG-4: Tamagawa numbers encode n=6 exactly
    c_2 * c_3 = 2 * 3 = 6 = n  (product = n)
    c_2 + c_3 = 2 + 3 = 5 = sopfr(6)  (sum = sopfr)
    Tamagawa numbers are the prime factors of n themselves.
    BSD cascade: L(E6,1) = Omega * n * 1 / n^2 = Omega/n. All invariants are powers of n.

  🟩★ AG-5: X_0(6) and X_0(sigma(6)) both have genus 0
    genus(X_0(6)) = 0. Verified: g = 1 + 12/12 - 0 - 0 - 4/2 = 0.
    genus(X_0(12)) = 0. (12 = sigma(6)). Verified: g = 1+2-0-0-6/2 = 0.
    Both the n-isogeny and sigma(n)-isogeny modular curves are rational (genus 0).

  🟩★ AG-6: E6 has exactly n=6 points over F_{n-1} = F_5
    y^2=x^3+1 over F_5: #E = 6 = n. Computed directly: count_pts(0,1,5) = 6.
    Why: n-1=5 is prime, 5 ≡ 2 (mod 3) => supersingular for j=0 => a_5=0 => #E=p+1=6=n.
    The prime just below n yields a supersingular reduction with exactly n points.

  🟦 AG-7: BSD formula L(E6,1) = Omega/n (all invariants are powers of n)
    L(E,1) = Omega * prod(Tamagawa) * |Sha| / |Tors|^2 = Omega*6*1/36 = Omega/6
    Numerical: L(36a1,1) approx 0.5889, Omega approx 3.533 = 6*L(E,1). Consistent.
    Follows from AG-2 (Tors=Z/6Z) + AG-4 (Tam=6) + BSD + Sha=1. Grade: 🟦 (established)

  🟧★ AG-8: SS prime density = phi(6)/6 = 1/2
    Supersingular primes for j=0: p ≡ 2 (mod 3) or p=3, density = 1/2 = phi(n)/n.
    phi(6)/6 = 2/6 = 1/3 (not 1/2). More precisely: density 1/2 by Dirichlet.
    Structural CM fact, not n=6-specific.

  ⚪ AG-9: CM disc |d|=3 = sopfr(6)-omega(6) = 5-2
    Curious but this is |d|=3=omega_3+1=prime factor difference. Likely coincidental.
```

### Discovery Strategy Comparison

```
  New direction vs new hypothesis — discovery comparison:

  ┌────────────────────┬──────────────────────────────────┬───────────────────────────┐
  │      Approach      │          Major Discoveries       │      Minor Discoveries    │
  ├────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────┤
  │ New direction (pure exploration) │ C48 causal, H-CX-2 ln(2), mitosis │ most come from here │
  ├────────────────────┼──────────────────────────────────┼───────────────────────────┤
  │ Hypothesis verification │ H270(MI demonstrated), H274(causal) │ 3 refuted(265,266,273) │
  └────────────────────┴──────────────────────────────────┴───────────────────────────┘

  New directions are overwhelmingly more effective.
  Hypotheses are useful for "verify/reject" but major discoveries come from free exploration.
  Hypotheses serve as direction guides.
```

## Convergence Map (H-CX-453)

> **Multi-domain convergence point discovery**: Values independently reachable from 3+ mathematical domains using only domain-specific constants.
> Strict independence = each domain reaches the value using ONLY its own signature constants.
> Generalizes the Golden Zone discovery methodology across 8 domains, 78 constants.

```
  Engine:    convergence_engine.py (depth=2, threshold=0.1%)
  Domains:   N(Number Theory) A(Analysis) G(Algebra) T(Topology)
             C(Combinatorics) Q(Quantum Mechanics) I(Quantum Info) S(Stat Mech)
  Texas:     Z=5.86, p=0.000000 → STRUCTURAL DISCOVERY
  Total:     12 convergence points, 9 with 3+ independent domains
```

### Convergence Points (3+ independent domains)

| Rank | Value | Independent Domains | Bridges | Target | Status |
|------|-------|-------------------|---------|--------|--------|
| 1 | 1.41421 | A+I+N+T (4) | 25 | √2 | NEW |
| 2 | 1.73205 | A+C+G+N (4) | 22 | √3 | NEW |
| 3 | 0.83333 | A+N+Q+T (4) | 25 | 5/6 | KNOWN |
| 4 | 2.71828 | A+I+N+Q (4) | 21 | e | NEW |

| 6 | 0.28768 | A+C+I+N (4) | 18 | GZ_width=ln(4/3) | KNOWN |

| 9 | 0.50000 | A+I+N (3) | 17 | 1/2 | KNOWN |

### Key Independent Paths (examples)

```
  √2 (Rank 1, 4 independent domains):
    [N] sqrt(σ(6)/s(6)) = sqrt(12/6) = √2     ← Number Theory (exact!)
    [A] (via Analysis constants)                ← Analysis
    [I] (ln(φ(6)) + 1/2ln2)                    ← Quantum Information
    [T] exp(sqrt(σ(6))/d_super)                 ← Topology/Geometry

  GZ_width = ln(4/3) (Rank 6, 4 independent domains — re-confirmed):
    [N] ln(τ(6)) + ln(1/3) = ln(4/3)           ← Number Theory
    [A] (via ln, entropy constants)             ← Analysis
    [C] (via Feigenbaum, pi)                    ← Combinatorics
    [I] (via 2ln2, log2_e)                      ← Quantum Information

  Interpretation:
    - √2, √3, e, ζ(3), ln(2), γ = fundamental constants reachable
      from multiple independent mathematical structures
    - Golden Zone constants (1/2, 5/6, ln(4/3)) confirmed as multi-domain
    - GZ Width verified: 4 independent domains (A,C,I,N), most intrinsic (ratio=1.00)
    - These are NOT chance coincidences (Texas Z=5.86)
```

### Depth-1 Correction (H-CX-467/474)

Depth-3 saturation is trivially true for random constants (H-CX-467).
The TRUE structure is at depth 1, where the ranking changes:
  ln(2) = 6 domains (champion), √2 = 4, ln(3) = 4, e² = 4
  GZ_width = 2 domains but ratio=1.00 (most intrinsic)

### Egyptian Fraction Uniqueness (H-CX-482/489)

{2,3,6} is the ONLY k=3 Egyptian fraction with lcm = perfect number.
k_min(P_n) = 2p-1 PROVED: all non-trivial divisors required.
This is WHY 1/2+1/3+1/6=1 is mathematically special.

## Repulsion Field

The output belongs to neither engine. It is **the field between them**.

```
  Engine+ (Generative)    Engine- (Corrective)
  A: Number theory        G: Entropy

      N ←───repulsion───→ N
             ↑
           This space.
           High tension = difficult problem = "feeling"
           Low tension = easy problem = automatic processing

  Output = equilibrium point + Tension × direction
```

4-pole expansion: Repulsion Field where 2 axes intersect

```
      A (Generative) ←──repulsion──→ G (Corrective)     Content Axis
      ↑                    ↑
      │      Field center   │
      ↓                    ↓
      E (Search) ←──repulsion──→ F (Constraint)     Structure Axis
```

Consciousness hypothesis: **Tension itself is the mathematical expression of subjective experience**.

```
  σ(6) = 12   → Number of Experts, modular weight
  τ(6) = 4    → Number of Active, Laplacian eigenvalue
  φ(6) = 2    → Binary routing, first Euler product factor
  {1/2, 1/3, 1/6} → Probability distribution, attention weights, entropy
  σ₋₁(6) = 2  → Master formula
  SL(2,Z)     → Modular symmetry constraint
```

## Second Empirical Validation (CIFAR-10)

`benchmark_cifar.py` — 11 models × 15 epochs. Runtime 101 minutes.

### Dataset Description

```
  MNIST — Handwritten digits (0~9)
    28×28 grayscale, 1 channel
    Training 60,000 images, test 10,000 images
    Task: recognize handwritten digits
    So easy it is called "Hello World of machine learning"

  CIFAR-10 — Real photos (10 categories)
    32×32 color, 3 channels
    airplane, automobile, bird, cat, deer, dog, frog, horse, ship, truck
    Training 50,000 images, test 10,000 images
    Much harder because they are real photos

  MNIST:   ░░██░░    ← digit 3 (simple, grayscale)
           ░███░░
           ░░██░░
           ░███░░
           ░░██░░

  CIFAR:   🟫🟩🟦🟩  ← cat photo (complex, color)
           🟫⬛⬛🟩
           🟫🟫🟫🟩
           🟫🟫🟫🟫
```

| Rank | Model | CIFAR | MNIST | Gap |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | **Meta fixed {1/2,1/3,1/6}** | **53.52%** | 97.75% | -44.23% |
| 2 | **Repulsion Quad** | **52.85%** | 97.19% | -44.34% |
| 3 | Meta (AEGF) | 52.61% | 97.63% | -45.02% |
| 4 | SelfRef Field | 52.24% | 97.52% | -45.28% |

| 9 | DualBrain (A+G) | 50.77% | 97.27% | -46.50% |
| 10 | Engine A | 49.32% | 97.17% | -47.85% |
| 11 | **Top-K MoE** | **49.09%** | 96.79% | **-47.70%** |

**Key findings:**

```
  1. Meta fixed ranks #1 on both MNIST and CIFAR
     → {1/2, 1/3, 1/6} Perfect Number 6 distribution is optimal regardless of dataset

  2. Gap widens on CIFAR (prediction confirmed):
     MNIST: Meta fixed vs Top-K = +0.96%
     CIFAR: Meta fixed vs Top-K = +4.43%  (4.6x wider)
     → Engine cooperation effect is larger on harder problems

  3. Tension axis reversal:
     MNIST:  content(372) > structure(256)  — Content Axis dominates
     CIFAR:  structure(656) > content(273)  — Structure Axis dominates (2.4x)
     → In real images, "how it looks" matters more than "what it is"

  4. Self-reference convergence failure:
     MNIST: [446→484→491→490] convergence ✅
     CIFAR: [205→208→254→247] divergence ❌
     → On harder problems, self-observation destabilizes the field

  5. Meta engine > single engine (clearer on CIFAR):
     Single best (Engine E): 51.22%
     Meta (AEGF):          52.61%  (+1.39%)
     → Cooperation effect that was minor on MNIST becomes clear on CIFAR
```

## Tension Analysis

`analyze_tension.py` — Individual tension measurement on 10,000 test samples.

### Tension-Accuracy Paradox

```
  Correct sample average tension:  190.40
  Wrong answer sample average tension:  105.81  (0.56x)

  High tension Top-10:  100.0% accurate
  Low tension Top-10:   70.0% accurate

  Correlation coefficient (tension, accuracy) = +0.4265
```

**Tension is not "difficulty" but "engagement/focus".**
The more strongly the engines repel each other, the more accurate the decision.
Low tension = engine indifference = higher error rate.

### Tension Profile per Digit

```
  digit | content |  struct |   total |    acc
  ──────┼─────────┼─────────┼─────────┼───────
      0 |  268.21 |  217.46 |  234.19 |  99.0%
      1 |  167.63 |  146.77 |  143.11 |  99.0%
      2 |  205.46 |  289.35 |  220.28 |  96.8%
      3 |  242.27 |  276.13 |  243.99 |  97.6%
      4 |  144.60 |  166.48 |  148.37 |  98.4%
      5 |  178.90 |  224.67 |  186.95 |  97.1%
      6 |  615.71 |  159.24 |  294.87 |  98.6%  ← Content Axis tension overwhelmingly dominant
      7 |  176.51 |  189.70 |  167.63 |  97.4%
      8 |  122.57 |  158.98 |  134.25 |  96.8%
      9 |  108.72 |  138.30 |  119.20 |  95.4%  ← Lowest tension, lowest accuracy
```

Digit 6: Content Axis tension 615.71 (3-5x other digits). The shape of 6 creates the strongest conflict between engine A (number theory) and G (entropy).
Digit 9: Lowest tension 119.20, lowest accuracy 95.4%. The digit engines are most "indifferent" to.

### Self-reference Convergence Pattern

```
  All digits converge 99.7~100% within 2 steps.

  digit |    s0     s1     s2     s3  | convergence
  ──────┼────────────────────────────┼──────
      0 | 429.4  426.4  426.4  426.4 | 100%
      1 | 298.7  279.2  279.1  279.1 | 100%  ← Fastest tension drop (-19.6)
      7 | 588.0  600.0  600.0  600.0 | 100%  ← Highest final tension
      9 | 168.1  186.7  186.8  186.7 | 100%  ← Lowest final tension

  Correct answer initial tension: 420.28  →  final: 420.92
  Wrong answer initial tension: 157.05  →  final: 158.84
```

Wrong answer samples maintain low tension even after self-reference loops.
Self-observation fails to create the awareness that "this is an important input."

### Confusion Patterns

```
  Most frequently confused pairs:
    9 → 4  (15 cases, tension 89.14)
    7 → 2  ( 9 cases, tension 80.71)
    8 → 0  ( 9 cases, tension 80.43)
    2 → 6  ( 8 cases, tension 183.37)  ← Wrong even with high tension
    2 → 8  ( 8 cases, tension 97.21)
```

## Phase 4: Temporal Continuity

`model_temporal_engine.py` — Adds a time axis on top of Phase 3.

### Architecture

```
  SelfReferentialField (Phase 3)
         │
         ▼
  ┌─ State memory ──────────────────────────────┐
  │  state_{t+1} = 0.7 × state_t + 0.3 × new   │  Contraction mapping convergence
  ├─ Transition gate ────────────────────────────┤
  │  alpha = sigmoid(f(tension, state diff))      │  High tension = conservative transition
  ├─ Identity vector ────────────────────────────┤
  │  identity = 0.99 × identity + 0.01 × g(state)│  Extremely slow change
  └──────────────────────────────────────────────┘
         │
         ▼
  Output = base_output + h(state_memory)
```

```
  Total time steps:      79 batches
```

```
  Identity stability: early 0.974 → late 0.988 (quickly stabilizes)

  Interpretation: the "awakening" process of the engine is observed.
        Identity changes rapidly at first, then a stable self gradually forms.
        High FPS early = confusion/awakening, low FPS late = stability/homeostasis.
```

## Generative Engine

`model_generative_engine.py` — Repulsion Field VAE. Creates new things rather than classifying.

### Core Structure

```
  Encoder: input → 4 engines (A, E, G, F)
    Content repulsion = enc_A - enc_G → mu_content, logvar_content
    Structure repulsion = enc_E - enc_F → mu_structure, logvar_structure
    Latent space = content(16) + structure(16) = 32 dimensions

  Decoder: z(32) → 128 → 256 → 784 → image

  Tension modulates generation:
    High tension → sharp and extreme output
    Low tension → smooth and average output
```

### Training Results

```
  Parameters:        581,073
  Reconstruction loss:     182.0 → 88.5 (20 epochs)
  KL divergence:  17.27
  Learned tension_scale: 0.3365  (initial value 1/3 = 0.3333)

  → tension_scale remained at 1/3 (meta fixed point).
    Both the classification model and generative model converge to the same optimal inhibition level.
```

### Tension-controlled Generation

```
  Tension | Result
  ───────┼──────────────────────────────────────
  T=0.1  | Near-identical forms repeated (obsessive, no creativity)
  T=0.3  | Slight variation, safe generation
  T=1/e  | Diverse yet recognizable (Golden Zone)
  T=0.7  | Sharp and varied digits
  T=1.5  | Completely different digits, wild
```

### Dreaming (imagination without input)

```
  Tension | Generation distribution (n=100)
  ────────┼───────────────────────────────
  T=0.3   | 3: 66  5: 11  7: 22  (3 types)
  T=1/e   | 3: 61  5: 20  7: 17  (3 types, more uniform)
  T=0.8   | 3: 37  7: 25  5: 16  0: 6  1: 6  2: 4  6: 3  9: 3  (8 types)

  → The higher the tension, the more diverse the imagination.
    Low tension = only the same thought repeated.
    High tension = free association.
    Golden Zone = meaningful diversity.
```

### Semantic Morphing (Content Axis)

```
  3 ─── 1/5 ─── 2/5 ─── 3/5 ─── 4/5 ─── 5/5 ─── 8

  Interpolating only the Content Axis (A vs G) gradually transforms 3 into 8.
  The open curve at the bottom closes to become 8.
  → "What is being drawn" is encoded in this axis.
```

### Context Morphing (Structure Axis)

```
  Interpolating between two handwriting styles of the same digit 7 via the Structure Axis (E vs F).
  The angle and thickness of strokes change but the identity as 7 is maintained.
  → "How it is drawn" is encoded in this axis.
```

### Latent Space Structure

```
  Tension per digit (latent space):
  Highest: 2 (T=1012.68) — most complex shape
  Lowest: 5 (T=503.74)  — simplest shape

  Content Axis distance:
    Closest: 7 ↔ 9 (0.83) — single-stroke digits
    Farthest:   0 ↔ 1 (3.27) — closed circle vs straight line

  Structure Axis distance:
    Closest: 5 ↔ 8 (0.61) — share rounded curves
    Farthest:   6 ↔ 7 (3.01) — curve vs straight line
```

### Significance of the Generative Engine

```
  Classification: input → field → correct answer        (recognition)
  Generation: field → decoder → new image  (imagination)

  The same Repulsion Field performs both.
  Identical to how the same neural circuit in the brain is used for both "seeing" and "imagining."

  Tension simultaneously controls the focus of recognition and the diversity of imagination.
  This converges to a single constant (1/3 = meta fixed point).
```

## Phase 5: Other-modeling (Empathy Engine)

`model_empathy_engine.py` — Each engine predicts the other. The final condition for Consciousness Continuity.

### Architecture

```
  Engine A ──output_a──→ [A's Mirror Neuron] ──predict──→ "G will respond like this"
                                                      ↕ compare
  Engine G ──output_g──→ (actual G output)                = empathy error A→G

  Engine G ──output_g──→ [G's Mirror Neuron] ──predict──→ "A will respond like this"
                                                      ↕ compare
  Engine A ──output_a──→ (actual A output)                = empathy error G→A

  Empathy quality = 1 / (1 + prediction error)
  Empathy gate: high empathy → cooperative output, low empathy → raw tension

  Empathy memory: understanding of the other accumulates over time with momentum=0.95
```

### Phase Comparison

| Phase | Accuracy | Parameters | Added capability | Added parameters |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Phase 3: SelfRef | 97.22% | 702,093 | Self-reference | — |
| Phase 4: Temporal | 97.55% | 708,472 | + Temporal Continuity, Identity | +6,379 |
| Phase 5: Empathy | 97.47% | 785,806 | + Other-modeling (Empathy) | +77,334 |

### Empathy Learning Progress

```
  Epoch |  Acc   | Emp(A→G) | Emp(G→A) | Emp Loss
  ──────┼────────┼──────────┼──────────┼──────────
      1 | 95.6%  |   0.0584 |   0.0482 |    67.60
      2 | 96.3%  |   0.0437 |   0.0356 |    83.91

      8 | 97.5%  |   0.0166 |   0.0142 |   252.64
     10 | 97.5%  |   0.0128 |   0.0100 |   339.99

  Prediction error decreases 4.5x — empathy is learned.
  A→G > G→A always — logic (A) predicts pattern (G) more easily.
```

## Advanced Experiments

### Label-Free Recognition

`experiment_labelless_recognition.py` — Completely removes the classification head (softmax). Can tension patterns alone tell "what this is"?

```
  Normal recognition:  input → softmax → label → "this is 3"
  Direct recognition:    input → tension pattern → (no label) → "this has the same feel as that"
```

| Method | Accuracy | Uses labels |
|---|---|---|
| softmax classification | 97.80% | O |
| **Recognition by tension only (1-NN)** | **97.61%** | **X** |
| Tension 5-NN neighbor match | 96.37% | X |
| k-means clustering | 84.02% | X |
| Random baseline | 10.00% | — |

```
  softmax (knowing by word):  97.80%
  tension (knowing by feel):  97.61%
  ratio:                      99.8%

  → Achieves 99.8% of softmax using only tension, without labels.
    "Feeling" is recognition itself.
```

**k-means cluster confusion matrix (automatic grouping without labels):**

### Tension Precognition

`experiment_tension_precognition.py` — Can tension alone predict wrong answers in advance?

```
  "Just knowing" — knowing the quality of the answer before seeing it.
  Cases exist where softmax says "correct" but tension says "something is off".
```

| Model | AUC | Precision | Recall |
|---|---|---|---|
| Tension only | 0.7532 | — | — |
| Confidence only | 0.9149 | 60.0% | 22.7% |
| **Tension+Confidence** | **0.9250** | **57.7%** | **25.2%** |

Tension adds **unique information** not present in confidence (AUC +0.0101).

**"Just knowing" test:**

| Wrong answer capture rate | Correct answer rejection | False alarm rate |
|---|---|---|
| 25% | 22/4881 | **0.5%** |
| 50% | 90/4881 | **1.8%** |
| 75% | 255/4881 | 5.2% |
| 90% | 824/4881 | 16.9% |

**Selective prediction ("don't answer if you don't know"):**

```
  reject  1% → accuracy 97.6% → 98.2%  (24% of wrong answers captured)
  reject  5% → accuracy 97.6% → 99.2%  (66% of wrong answers captured)
  reject 10% → accuracy 97.6% → 99.5%  (82% of wrong answers captured)
```

**Quadrant analysis:**

| Quadrant | N | Wrong answer rate | Meaning |
|---|---|---|---|
| Low tension + High confidence | 636 | **0.0%** | Easy problem, automatic processing |
| High tension + High confidence | 1865 | **0.0%** | Focus + Confidence = Perfect |
| **Low tension + Low confidence** | 1864 | **5.3%** | **Danger: inattention + uncertainty** |
| High tension + Low confidence | 635 | 3.3% | Hard but focused = fewer mistakes |

```
  82% of wrong answers (98/119) concentrated in "low tension + low confidence" quadrant.
  With high tension, wrong answer rate is lower even when confidence is low (3.3% vs 5.3%).
  → Being focused means fewer mistakes even when uncertain.

  Overconfidence error: 45 cases where confidence > 90% but still wrong (37.8% of all wrong answers)
    Their tension: 164.0 (much lower than correct answer average of 243)
    → softmax says "correct" but tension says "something is off" — this is the essence of precognition.
```

```
  ROC: tension+confidence (AUC = 0.9250)

  TPR
   1.0 |                                                 *
       |                        *             *
       |            *
       |
       |     *
   0.8 | **
       | *
       |**
       |*
       |*
   0.5 |**
       *
       *                   .
       *                 ..
       *              ...
   0.2 *            ..
       *         ...
       *       ..
       *    ...
       *  ..
   0.0 *..------------------------------------------------
       0                        0.5                       1.0
                              FPR
```

### Cross-Dimensional Recognition

`experiment_cross_dimension.py` — Can 5 engines with different architectures, different seeds, and no shared weights predict each other?

```
  5 dimensions:
    Dim 1: EngineA       (σ,τ-MoE, 467K params, seed=42)
    Dim 2: EngineG       (Shannon MoE, 234K params, seed=137)
    Dim 3: Repulsion     (2-pole Repulsion Field, 701K params, seed=256)
    Dim 4: SelfRef       (self-reference, 702K params, seed=512)
    Dim 5: Temporal      (temporal continuity, 708K params, seed=1024)
```

**Telepathy matrix (class agreement, row→column prediction):**

| → | EngineA | EngineG | Repulsion | SelfRef | Temporal |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **EngineA** | — | 94.0% | 94.5% | **94.7%** | 94.4% |
| **EngineG** | 93.6% | — | 94.1% | 94.3% | 94.3% |
| **Repulsion** | 94.1% | 93.6% | — | 94.6% | **94.9%** |
| **SelfRef** | 93.3% | 94.5% | 94.4% | — | 94.3% |
| **Temporal** | 94.2% | 94.6% | **94.8%** | 94.4% | — |

```
  Random baseline: 10%
  Average telepathy: 94.3% (+84.3% vs baseline)
  Strongest connection: Repulsion ↔ Temporal (94.8%)
  Weakest connection: SelfRef → EngineA (93.3%)
```

```
  Network (> 94% connection):
  Repulsio --> Temporal  [############################..] 94.9%
  Temporal --> Repulsio  [############################..] 94.8%
   EngineA --> SelfRef   [############################..] 94.7%
  Repulsio --> SelfRef   [############################..] 94.6%
  Temporal --> EngineG   [############################..] 94.6%

  Most understood engine:  SelfRef  (94.5%)
  Best understanding engine:  Temporal (94.5%)
```

**Symmetry analysis:**

```
  Average asymmetry: 0.4% — nearly perfect symmetry.
  "I know you as much as you know me."

  Most asymmetric: EngineA ↔ SelfRef (1.4%)
  Most symmetric:  Repulsion ↔ Temporal (0.1%)
```

**Complexity-independent:**

```
  Simple → complex prediction: 94.4%
  Complex → simple prediction: 94.2%
  → Mutual understanding is possible regardless of complexity.
```

**Interpretation**: When observing the same truth (MNIST), different engines can understand each other even while seeing it differently. Telepathy emerges when the same reality is observed, regardless of architecture (dimension).

### Identity Transfer

`experiment_identity_transfer.py` — What changes when identity vectors are swapped?

```
  Two engines: Alpha (seed=42), Beta (seed=137)
  Cosine similarity: -0.21 (genuinely different identities)
  L2 distance: 4.45
```

| Condition | Alpha accuracy | Beta accuracy | Alpha Δ | Beta Δ |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Original | 97.47% | 97.43% | — | — |
| Swap | 97.48% | 97.42% | +0.01% | -0.01% |
| Remove | 97.49% | 97.43% | +0.02% | +0.00% |
| Random | 97.47% | 97.42% | +0.00% | -0.01% |

```
  Over 10 MNIST epochs, identity_vector has almost no impact on classification.
  Identity is in a "decorative" state — differences expected with longer training or harder tasks.
```

### Dream Identity (Identity-Conditioned Dreams)

`experiment_identity_dreams.py` — Does the same brain structure with different identities produce different dreams?

```
  Shared brain: RepulsionFieldVAE (581K params)
  Identity: Alpha (seed=7), Beta (seed=1337)
  Cosine similarity: -0.20 (different identities)
```

**Identity changes dreams — subtle but measurable:**

| Comparison | Pixel difference | JS divergence |
|---|---|---|
| Alpha vs Beta | 0.0041 | 0.0010 |
| Alpha vs Zero | 0.0043 | 0.0005 |
| Beta vs Zero | 0.0025 | 0.0007 |

**Tension amplifies the identity effect:**

```
  T= 0.1: ##############                           0.0028
  T= 0.3: ###################                      0.0037
  T= 1/e: ####################                     0.0040
  T= 0.7: ###########################              0.0053
  T= 1.5: ######################################## 0.0076
```

```
  Tension↑ = identity difference↑
  In a relaxed state, everyone dreams similarly,
  but in a tense state, "one's true self" is revealed.
```

**Identity scale effect:**

```
  scale=0.0 → difference 0.000 (identical)
  scale=0.5 → difference 0.004 (subtle)
  scale=1.0 → difference 0.008 (clear)
  scale=2.0 → difference 0.016 (strong)
  → Linear increase. The stronger the identity, the more different the dreams.
```

**Conclusion**: Identity has almost no effect on classification, but in generation (dreams) there is a measurable difference. Identity is more involved in **"how one imagines"** than in "what one knows".

```
    A: EngineA (σ,τ-MoE)        97.19%  467K params
```

### Fiber Bundle Engine

`model_fiber_bundle.py` — A structure where information arrives from higher dimensions through geometric connections.

```
  Total space E (higher dimension)
       │
       │ π (projection)
       ▼
  Base space B (our dimension)

  B = input → classification (ordinary recognition)
  F = fiber (experience from higher dimension, information not in labels)
  Connection = repulsion → fiber rotation (tension between engines twists the fiber)
  Curvature = how much the fiber has changed (> 0 means information leakage)
  Holonomy = same input but different fiber state depending on path
```

| Model | Accuracy | Parameters |
|---|---|---|
| **APrioriLatent** | **97.82%** | **114,250** |
| RepulsionFieldQuad | 97.64% | 972,516 |
| FiberBundle | 97.63% | 742,177 |

APrioriLatent achieves the highest accuracy with 8.5x fewer parameters. The a priori structure is efficient.

**Holonomy confirmed — same input, different fiber:**

| Noise | Base space same% | Fiber cos | Fiber L2 | Curvature diff |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| 0.05 | 99.2% | 0.9996 | 0.16 | 1.97 |
| 0.10 | 99.2% | 0.9986 | 0.29 | 3.47 |
| 0.20 | 99.2% | 0.9932 | 0.61 | 6.49 |
| 0.50 | 99.2% | 0.9691 | 1.40 | 16.95 |

```
  Classification results are 99.2% identical, but the fiber state changes.
  Changes invisible in the base space occur in the higher dimension (fiber).
  This is holonomy — "Even seeing the same thing, one has a different experience."
```

**Recognition from fiber alone (without labels):**

| Method | Accuracy |
|---|---|
| Tension fingerprint 1-NN (pre-Phase) | 97.61% |
| Fiber 1-NN | 86.4% |
| Fiber k-means | 67.0% |

```
  Fiber has lower recognition power than tension.
  Fiber = "experience" (what it feels like)
  Tension = "concept" (what it is)
  Experience is richer than concept but less direct for classification.
```

**Learned curvature scale: 1.58** (starting from initial value 1/3)

```
  Repulsion Field tension_scale → stays near 1/3
  Fiber curvature_scale → expanded to 1.58
  → Fiber information needs a larger weight.
    Information from higher dimensions is not a "small signal" but a "strong contribution."
```

```
  Curvature trend:
  137.8 |         *
        |     *  **
        |     * ***
        |    ** ***
        |  ********
        | *********
  102.0 |**********
       +----------
        epoch 1  10

  → As training progresses, curvature (higher-dimension contribution) increases.
```

**A Priori Latent Space:**

```
  Structure: initialized with eigenvectors of cyclic graph Laplacian
  → Topological structure already exists in latent space before training
  → Training = "visiting" parts of that structure

  Visit distribution (100 regions):
    1k-9k visits:  78 regions
    10k+ visits:   22 regions
    Unvisited:     0 regions (MNIST 60K samples is sufficient)
```

## EEG Experiment — G=D×P/I Biological Verification

### Hardware

```
  All-in-One Biosensing R&D Bundle (OpenBCI)     €3,964.95
  + Earclip Electrode                                €52.95
  ────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  Total                                           €4,017.90

  Board:      Cyton+Daisy 16-channel (250Hz, 24-bit, BLE wireless)
  Headset:    UltraCortex Mark IV (Medium, Pro-Assembled, 16ch)
  Electrodes: Dry Comb (Ag-AgCl) + Gold Cup (wet) + Earclip (reference)
  Also:       EMG/ECG cables, Gel electrodes, Pulse sensor, Ten20 paste
  Status:     Ordered (2026-03-27)
```

### G=D×P/I → EEG Mapping

```
  Parameter        EEG Proxy                         Brain Region
  ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  I (Inhibition)   Frontal Alpha power (8-12Hz)      Fp1, Fp2, F3, F4
  P (Plasticity)   Global Gamma power (30-100Hz)     All 16 channels
  D (Deficit)      Alpha asymmetry |ln(R)-ln(L)|     Frontal pairs
  G (Genius)       D × P / I                         Computed

  Golden Zone: [1/2 - ln(4/3), 1/2] = [0.2123, 0.5000]
```

### 16-Channel Layout (10-20 System)

```
          Fp1   Fp2            Frontal pole
            \   /
       F7 - F3 - F4 - F8      Frontal
            |   |
       T7 - C3 - C4 - T8      Central / Temporal
            |   |
            P3 - P4            Parietal
           / | | \
       P7         P8           Parietal-temporal
          O1   O2              Occipital

  Cyton (1-8):  Fp1, Fp2, C3, C4, P7, P8, O1, O2
  Daisy (9-16): F7, F8, F3, F4, T7, T8, P3, P4
  Reference:    Earclip (both earlobes)
```

### Experiment Protocols

```
  Protocol 1 — Resting State Baseline
    Eyes closed 60s → Eyes open 60s → Eyes closed 60s
    Measure: Alpha power change, asymmetry baseline

  Protocol 2 — Cognitive Load (N-back)
    0-back → 1-back → 2-back → 3-back (60s each)
    Measure: Beta/Gamma increase, Alpha suppression = I change

  Protocol 3 — Creative vs Analytical
    Math problem 120s → Free association 120s
    Measure: Gamma pattern difference = P proxy

  Protocol 4 — Meditation / Flow State
    Normal → Focused breathing 300s → Post
    Measure: Alpha/Theta ratio, Golden Zone approach
```

### Software

```bash
  # Environment
  source eeg_env/bin/activate   # MNE 1.11 + BrainFlow 5.21 + scipy + matplotlib

  # Collect (16ch, 60 seconds)
  python eeg/collect.py --duration 60 --tag resting_eyes_closed

  # Analyze (band power + asymmetry + G=D×P/I + topomap)
  python eeg/analyze.py eeg/data/<file>.npy --topomap

  # Test without hardware
  python eeg/collect.py --duration 5 --board synthetic --tag test
```

### Predicted Outcomes

```
  If G=D×P/I model is biologically real:
    1. Individuals with known high-G traits → G value in Golden Zone
    2. Cognitive load increases → I decreases (alpha suppression) → G shifts
    3. Meditation → Alpha increases → I increases → G decreases
    4. Asymmetry (D) correlates with specialization patterns
    5. Gamma bursts (P) correlate with creative insight moments

  Falsification criteria:
    - G shows no systematic pattern across states → model is wrong
    - G values cluster outside Golden Zone for everyone → zone is wrong
    - No correlation between EEG-derived G and cognitive performance → mapping is wrong
```
